## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population P and time t, which is the fundamental ODE formulation in population dynamics. The relationship likely involves density-dependent growth mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below critical threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + P) (reduced growth at low density without extinction threshold)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Time-varying Malthusian: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponential growth with time-varying rate)
- Logistic with time-dependent capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (carrying capacity changing over time)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (simplest polynomial density-dependent model)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (Allee-type polynomial model)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (hyperbolic density dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP/dt is proportional to P at low densities but curves downward at high P → logistic-type density dependence (quadratic in P)
- If dP/dt is negative at both very low AND very high P → Allee effect requiring cubic terms in P
- If the growth rate per capita (dP_dt / P) decreases linearly with P → classic logistic model
- If the growth rate per capita decreases nonlinearly/convexly with P → theta-logistic or Gompertz model
- If residuals show systematic time trends after fitting P-only models → explicit time dependence in parameters (e.g., seasonal forcing or changing environment)
- Logarithmic dependence on P (log(P) terms) → Gompertz-type growth where per-capita rate declines logarithmically
- Ratio of polynomial terms in P (rational functions) → Holling-type functional responses or Beverton-Holt dynamics
- If dP/dt shows oscillatory behavior with t → consider sinusoidal time modulation c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t))
- If per-capita growth rate saturates rather than going negative → use rational fraction forms like c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) instead of polynomial
- Fractional power of P (P**c with 0<c<1) → sub-linear growth typical of surface-area-limited or diffusion-limited processes

GT = a*P - a*P*exp(-b*P) + a*P*exp(-b*t)

The candidate has `exp(P*c8)` but not `P*exp(P*c8)`. These are different. We need `P*exp(-bP)` but only have `exp(P*c8)`.
